## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard setup for ecological population-growth ODEs. With only (t, P) available, common structures include per-capita growth laws (functions of P) and nonautonomous forcing (explicit t-dependence) such as seasonality or time-varying environment/harvesting.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear time-trend in growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slow environmental drift affecting per-capita rate)
- Quadratic density dependence (logistic ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity-like saturation via crowding)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible density dependence; c2 tunes curvature near K)
- Gompertz-type regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (logarithmic density dependence; often used for microbial/forest stands)
- Generalized power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P ** c1 (allometric/sub- or super-linear scaling of growth with population size)
- Richards / generalized logistic (rational form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) ** c3 (extra shape control for approach to saturation)
- Allee effect (strong depensation, cubic form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low P plus carrying-capacity limitation)
- Density dependence via exponential crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (Ricker-like continuous-time inhibition)
- Net growth as difference of anabolic/catabolic scaling: dP_dt = c0 * P ** c1 - c2 * P ** c3 (von Bertalanffy-style or birthâ€“death scaling competition)
- Proportional harvesting/clearance: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to P, e.g., mortality/harvest)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P * sin(c3 * t + c4) (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P for small and moderate P, prefer multiplicative forms like P * f(t) (interpretable as per-capita rate).
- A negative P^2 term (or P*(1-c*P)) typically encodes crowding/competition and implies a stable equilibrium (carrying capacity).
- Sign changes in per-capita growth at low P (e.g., factors like (c*P-1)) indicate an Allee threshold where populations decline when rare.
- Log(P) appearing in dP_dt suggests Gompertz-type regulation where per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log population.
- An exp(-c*P) factor implies strong density dependence that ramps up quickly with P, often fitting sharp slowdowns at high density.
- Explicit sin(c*t+phi) terms indicate periodic forcing (seasonality) and can explain cyclic modulation of growth around a baseline.
- Separate additive removal terms (e.g., -c*P or -c0) indicate harvesting/mortality; whether it scales with P distinguishes proportional vs constant catch.
- Power-law exponents on P (P**c) can reflect scaling/allometry; exponents < 1 often model diminishing returns in growth with size.
